Mobile Vs. Desktop


Pandora reported better than expected (but still a loss) fiscal fourth quarter earnings late Thursday as the company continues to concentrate on a mobile future. See the release (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1jwU3HBdUybSejgo0Sn9R8NjSCTwgQi8x03_9tImLQ85Iub4jxEVtqlJ3DJv-iZ7AkRhWkdv0UhczmZZDl4dtn-MNbT6ePxG8rqZAzqcMaPfqINLYKz65coKDoD4LVcvMDz74nSyuAkIAxfp4X3JrQK7poNVdu6_G05CcE0d4x4t6ePeIGJjXVqyfiuZTKi5NfOzNmQZN5HkBd9jins0QJdR3XetCydiwM=> . The Wall Street Journal digs into the details, "Mobile ads still aren't as lucrative as those on traditional computers. The latter garnered $52.82 per 1,000 listening hours, compared with $25.05 for mobile." Read the WSJ (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1j-gKGbrGF_NueB48hDjA7H3JeS-jK-I4UHXFK-LUUs2tMzz5LkYrOPK4VgwCSoU7Ty_rfixrbmB_t3BuDXt5TbUBnm1W-bUUaKJBMtCSfG4_CId8Da1pF69dMxrgaYCyLXHPPz3o_LQx8lb_Gn-5CiZ-1L_Sn6bF_Wcm9vnYvtcuT6mY3d88aG> . The earnings call transcript discusses the Mediaocean and Strata integrations and where Triton Digital fits in for monetizing online radio. Read it (registration). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1gxKeIzJq5-ee_9tF_mteEUhNRQXHMvVRrxi9NXgDpjBJ2Pkok_emMGW4zQIpaY2RuylI5HbB2yla-RRvPcNjNjdy3kBJ3HcEor4u53DGl8mDOvSht-_FbJQgejvw6stQarbq3NSmcYLjIbfUtxCj0T0nOCEfeS7Q_dHivHVpbqe7zxL7NdOkqPTW2s832l6wkM5z69PuiHS6s_w1VcRisz97vhsBB3BW6hPBcTjdGb7oU25Fii_lOE> 


The Human Algo


Sure, technology is enabling plenty of ad targeting online and other areas of automated innovation, says The NY Times' Steve Lohr, but humans are still critical. He calls it the "man-machine collaboration" and references examples with IBM's Wason, Google and comparison engine FindTheBest. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1jTrHUyWqF-qhcSMbl5igeKr5SQYpK2_ClxS-QVZ_hnzWbge0_e7iyXiJBtbcJ03BhNMAs6CAUXTw0__CT05i9qr0_mMakiSyk37gA7XOe3RjFy0afEEfr4QTJQwU5aZo9W7HSZwuCisjlK-rLBqicfSNCwdyUeaRgbkZ6kGCB0fOhh1CaPQ4RZqavpF2Dx2aD8vylYYIi6P8O6QODuLMlgCtWmfi2PNXg=> 


Power To The First Party


Daniel Jaye, CEO of Korrelate, discusses the potential impact of Mozilla's decision to block third-party cookies that help track browsers and target advertising. Jaye tells Ad Age's Kate Kaye, "In the long run if this becomes adopted by [Google] Chrome and [Microsoft] IE ... you could see a world where the only data-enabled third party networks are those owned by the large first parties." Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1hzx-3rsR_Tvjmnpn2M-WMkK1izvuhvq3wy_viyb1PEX6h5reqM1CqSPcheQguD9e4-SO04TnIpWK0elpFtGoFhuzQvBH_TGaBuVf6PTDF14DITV9l0JfLpL8rWJ3BcbMx9ASRu79e_gLDkFcrKWcMpHL3kvYLu_RqQrTGJIbyvk0ZV_csok9ES> On Street Fight, former Korrelate-er Matt Sokoloff points out, "...advertisers and advertising technology companies have claimed that when a browser defaults a user's preferences to blocking third-party cookies, that isn't the same as a user opting out. This leaves the door open to some advertisers using cookieless tracking technology to continue to track users" - e.g. Akamai's "pixel-free" tech. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1j3SXfekfhLs49TFeNUilLgSxftwD-sYXKCXeWQNzwscuSjfkjejEEyWA4bsvSVJMI_2Tklv9-U0KJ3CaC5lly-8hm4yk7D31itFvPKQcO9Bo2QcJPvxn4pGhDNsbAT41yJ_gsmUyN_gmJur1mzDk3Fd4MvhmmcOx6HfPjuqARvAYjd_Y_kSV_dw3DHPOJFTBEMtj_VfMlH_Fy_K0hlJkwi>  Related from CNET <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1jK-1UEDFsycannywxbkCpzk8OkDNFUAP198ldcvNEldenXchl1yVV5YxYO6ZKmfNnExaf9hzlnSNV8lyzanj7KBU-HB70XVMgv4OfreJqx-xjMCV4gPfuWop0VYTLu-WJGf2udnDFEVr3ux77N-41IkaMTLjPKud2FhS-NgKAPAgJJ00j6dwgXwrmRHyd9-uo=> : Mozilla Says "No" To iOS. 


Media Storm


Media monger or branding genius? The Daily Beast's David Freedlander looks at the Weather Channel's relentless efforts to dominate weather forecasting. "In the world of media behemoths, the most voracious may well be the Weather Channel...The network, which grabbed the Weather.com domain back in the earliest days of the Internet, now draws some 163 million monthly unique visitors to its sites." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1h4m25_ZQgPFtrQ9N-4ICYfPfCB_cdHv511yzJL30ArJa77aOJA2FoDEyFRJla_HdIsswrgzMLuYx_UO3kkGXF1RYUbdGy1_tKg_JWfoQ4J45mqxZ_f_zaoWrh4GJo3smpUAXpszGZfM3EhrYrtNPrWZFg6Y-m2F-87cVMBuR4t5x4n8-wCOoplXyz_43SrUpptY_xO3ZFnqeh3IeALEsOkoMgyJ5-ojpw=> 


Fill It Up With Premium


Benjamin Humphry from audience targeting platform nugg.ad wades into the "programmatic premium" discussion courtesy of a think piece on eConsultancy. He offers, "Premium Programmatic is a noble goal, but it's a tough challenge, and innovation needs to happen before it can be considered solved." He's not a believer -yet. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001NC7GjQN2m1jZNzLdTix1_hDoXjZK9xrNbhxlWB5U_Z3yj8WflEcqGdECJi0X7aVmMQc16lAWhaIreC342gOrmymZWuJWk6fjcN5ntcA_tf4K-UhMNgY8VjtiCjUiuNnL9mpUO9IlfBXL_g4lk0YJljvfq7kIwx5VpBT_0sQzxNI=>

Bad Actors


On The Makegood, Casale Media's Andrew Casale reveals one way his company is finding "bad actors" among websites cranking through millions of ad impressions - the recency of the date a domain name was registered. He writes that one such site "had no audience in August 2012 yet two months later in October 2012 it was posting 400,000 unique users." Programmatic ESPN


Digiday's Josh Steinberg says that ESPN display inventory is appearing on exchanges at a $3 CPM as the sports media giant takes steps toward programmatic. ESPN media exec Lisa Valentino tells Steinberg, "Our core business is always going to be multimedia sponsorship,. (...) I really see this as a growing business, or we wouldn't have invested in it. But it's secondary to our core: content across every screen and translate that in meaningful ways for clients." Cox Chooses Collective 


As Cox Digital Solutions prepares to shut down <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSr-qaJp_4VV3sX_AfC0qbfOGCsuE4CY6QsnMftF-_ja2C8-ZXpDLI603kru4OZiqx3cYL5nsN4dfjZgeTeBX56o7XAp6tWUb4i7XhkZxhedv5fB0yWNmkRmeVkskInc7krp-6F9SuyYz4cMI_Q3p0OGdALvMuaXF1JGv5MFKPJMFDeTmRPJ6x9s-DzbS3pu-tcExKb5JRBYP0ek5bEJVbw_UrZmmP_eFY8Qye7LY76CV61TwEdIvV6o>  its in-house ad serving system, which evolved from its $300 million acquisition of white label ad network Adify four years ago, what's it planning to replace it with? The answer is Collective, which is being brought in to help target consumers as part of a wider re-org of CDS. The new program will be run by CoxReps, which also manages the Atlanta-based media company's TV ad sales network. ""Over the past several years, we've had big wins on both the broadcast and the digital side of the house," said CoxReps President Jim Monahan. "Independently, each is highly effective. But we've seen an industry shift toward converged solutions - coordinated advertising that reaches consumers anywhere they are, regardless of the medium. We plan to be one step ahead of that trend." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSr_RFLg0UhBqjofhhOvHmCMXeEheIj3itvyYP4DsVKvEfcluXZmixkzEdCUI4CMN7ivgDEb26WRoN_yUQSdrdYpU8Fi3xldg6eC-9UstGBFN_OJYUDurj2wuDmK_wyicICMD_n7PRNvF7Jqk8l55vvG95ohLxah-jTbSUjrNElWU4agrSjJpeSCqH4cGmWkZZWek-tWItPHq3DRsAs_Ux1E> . 


Facebook Data Risk


As Facebook re-architects Atlas, will advertisers balk at the prospect of sharing campaign data with a media seller? Pivotal Research analyst Brian Wieser thinks so. "How will agencies and advertisers who presently work with Atlas feel about a media owner controlling their ad serving and campaign management toolsuite, and using their information to sell other services back to them?" he writes in a research note covered by MediaPost. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSr9xtotQ3ybvNLgBRyVIbTxbAW_utWrdbXZRanW4GjFHDa9gRoEX5IDNmke3thgw40pyGWlxgPeZh1XxqfXQ2O8N5hiMt1NBz9jnwMmNJQkdZeSYK2Mrfir6pjsx18V0SS65V7Tr48A91yZL5f2YSEzxaPirjEu9B5cuwWBN6hsRVMBbFkRb1bJsbYQcljqXjAbIAKmpjeD_rqLLpk9r11rxP9OOnvBYe7e9zN3ErC06hrCOrrrQUFk> 


Premi-ammatic Progrium


If "programmatic premium" brings on cognitive dissonance, how about "systematic reserved," "guaranteed RTB" -- or just "process reform?" What to call this emerging category of exchange buying was on many lips at the IAB Annual Leadership Meeting, Chris O'Hara writes in a ClickZ column. "Maybe the term should be 'systematic reserved' for deals that happen when guaranteed buying platforms (like NextMark, Centro, and Mediaocean) plug into sell-side systems (like isocket, Adslot, and Shiny Ads) to enable a frictionless, tagless, IO-less buy." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSoA47NZVBwFPM0gZqOip4800XyVaV9HVaQXaegVJXCb0MMrGmwKQsLwwn0vjuq-IQzN-Hq9RXgEjcb-IOWaeZ_LczyowCYryfB3WE2pydywCWQPNz0wXh8Lh20Qc_wdV-4D5RFiEWpnIdvikXkbW_2LbZxyeGyWieRk4zuTaAfPV3Z3zsktcwbWxHM5ggTN2AGvrxoO1uAqJg==> 


Taming App Ads


In-app advertising is still the Wild West, but the IAB, MMA, and MRC are taking a shot at taming it with a new proposed set of "Mobile Application Advertising Measurement Guidelines." The document offers guidelines on in-app advertising, analytics, and more. A public comment period will last until April 6. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSqmevEsNYJxJEnAJyg6Xbpy0_PriSdW5hleI6o6rub7k5ryJpR_ChHSnWFrnMWvtM7ryL1bNjLAj6tHHehQL44rmmm4GDWQK05CfpZmDS42seFYp0wHMJkk8FPCulRdWn2hmtmqJ8mc6NJ458itVIVGAUeWexMGGaKK3-pSSMPlHCrRkt98dXo0-LhfS7m912m3J3Z-9nnyYHQIYmiy9EFSYXjXjHg8XONvW-0KDZsEFPCSsCBntMFgDe1LIGgqyPfSX6WHezz_N9d_uIigzHq0>  


Geo-Siege


Nine of 10 advertisers on the xAd mobile ad network are setting up geofences around competitor locations, Greg Sterling writes in the Screenwerk blog. An xAd exec tells Greg Sterling that national campaigns "often feature one type of ad creative to reach people around the companies' locations and a different approach and ad creative targeting consumers around competitors' locations." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSqynx-fw98N_MIt02BIMZIAeQOXlZ0wlj93kNJw8o97oULGRv5JGUTB1CvXjvzs40CLSR_UVCx6kDbLXOVKEbFPEooqLVkgnsijnIXZKza0wEjSVhWHXSptmfRKQherqAtFP1YFqPMa0-GVvkbhmlaWxToSRfqydeJfCUy_9KxcRoI4xidLd6zfOavwu13T0HF5Eui4YSpjHA==>  A potential downside of the geofence siege: French taunting. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSrI_IcUA7jqohkjKFx0OnD1YIbo4zGC2_OyIvuPF4Jlef7uaiC_wgNgJJxScDbhpdmpNNH3yV6Cjn5Rfp-Gl7tu5L4y9YIP0G9otb8eMWANNbmmZjA1p_yVsC7r2siZY8AQhNy_sH7zMA==>

Ad Games


Mobile ad startup Adcade is betting on a suite of rich media ad puzzles and games to keep users on brands' sites. "It's painfully clear that desktop ads don't translate well to mobile devices and, as mobile continues to grow, publishers need new solutions to monetize," The company just raised $1.5 million in seed funding. Radio Programmatic


Following yesterday's tie-up between online radio operator Pandora and Mediaocean, now Triton Digital, the digital services provider to traditional and online radio, has signed up CBS Radio to its a2x exchange programmatic system. "Joining Triton's a2x exchange will create additional demand for our inventory, providing a great compliment to our strong traditional sales channels," said Ezra Kucharz, President of CBS Local Digital Media. "Being able to offer agency trading desk access to our inventory in this manner allows us to participate in a new revenue stream targeting mobile and digital budgets." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSpIq4DY9th2I0t8qFh1WaGjYWHRaPcYvfiz9hIrAvZPJbd-uKrs_LQOGJuiXcpD7iQP594cGZ8YrIf1S2OcFCw3cQTVsIojuXfqFwLfz3LSoufWfJzkehR8Uy_8PXceSgfY08ogtgxqg5fGfExU27fzAlzKJ4oB8-zG9U-xNJHIcwrZOrVmx8tuCkBoFSgt5_bEYbJc1jjTOSM-J5q89OYNNiDPdD617TbkB_Sp-Z4l9g==> . 


Anti-Trust Bust


In spite of European Commission requirements, Microsoft has not provided for consumer choice when it comes to browser selection according a release yesterday by the Commission which provides oversight on anti-trust regulation. The EC said Microsoft would be fined 561 million fine and added: "This is the first time that the Commission has had to fine a company for non-compliance with a commitments decision." Read what that means. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001S_7JqQv6WSq_axzhD_4d0O929xv5GbVv0g8gMWxLz7JO08SjmQsU2ZIlYcTP6mLHD4VweNuSTfSYckzb2BtLqxrK_atMwl5zGn_2wSsX3cUg0kslTXidBRkI3nM83KknHrhA6LaedJ1azvWzqZfeURRGE3NHb-Ll>

The New Normal For Agencies


As companies founded on a traditional ad network model fail faster (see AdBrite <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAW6-jth0IVTDq-PrJHe6ZXdLWGkOzE0Xizm1MYV7K4M04JV90YgnV1BIHzFSjn7fQKEjWJEp6lQmDI6BHtgM6wl9CE1VMlFk-2HsDAqUU9TeqVTdE6WmVQtFI7r2Mak24HyqHvhMqIKC_iiQ2QJjvQwfuihoMLAWzblNdY3jVGMLlB4qAY709nSMX3XiFSNv1iT8H9x8fdv8tHS0FEeFlEaFSr-1UNLxqI=>  and Adify <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAV0fOpSjxzDuRKTA3cCj4EfZK3DoBQSupZ0EzqRVC1szGB-89bCXo8UCxoWccXPbmoCovIt7BH5RYwCaVs8SIjkEwV0kkuv6OhVUWZIFQ9_IE2EnWyMsT459gqOCuqJcovIz7rKTthm1QesPyg7B_ngN4b2uFExfbWdqeNzSiB3sIxuiP73vi5VoPa6YqqQlh9B8Cx2FrKOWA8vMBYMyH9GinHcGJZOPcE0TEJC1FUl6_8gM41umErw> ), one obvious factor is the dwindling of agency demand as budgets shift to programmatic. What does this look like from the inside? The Media Kitchen prez Barry Lowenthal outlines his company's transition to audience buying in a piece on AdWeek. A few years ago, he writes, "We started reducing the number of ad networks and direct site buys. That freed headspace to start focusing on the kinds of packages that an algorithm couldn't buy." So, more strategic thinking, not less. More <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAVC5kZRsUIn2YSmXB8Qa3y5b6sHPC8vXffaD0ddWlEVOG9-Rlp-FPwFDNF7bvrv6jktx2rUEF-27lUwpmmZxT-kSyZZzi2YZ6cSRvN6qwzoa_6Pu8e4brLKEOqxt7w6DYmgiiXHIwILZnTXASfO5iIyWUOLA88RR2z3cQQ_7Hq4aUsP4kP1VD0faAsOaEfNylBsTbQEefJW7VdNjo5_w0H3> 


Self Serve Social


Social ad firm SocialCode is automating more of its platform. A new self-serve version supports marketers that want to bring social campaign management in-house, including amplification of both paid and organic messaging. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAUxdNSetFzxUR6V0XrKA6b-9x6ztHakNY89pQIdrEHXSxvxqbtZYZ4nAUMI2IgwBStNJGBuENJyHNBcCMF8wRUOwBodtKHv_popt32jUk4if1j0Vx3V98KNaFAEWW5XibAzhlpN7Nkk9lOIoN58r73q> 


Mobile Ads for Tumblr


Brands will soon be able to push their Tumblr blogs and posts to the top of the stack on the microblogging site's mobile app, reports Bloomberg's Sarah Frier. "Tumblr Chief Executive Officer David Karp, who has expressed disdain for typical online display and search advertising, is betting he can achieve profitability simply by getting customers to pay to make their own posts stick out." AdExchanger's take: Like Facebook, Tumblr may find that the pay-to-play approach to native advertising could backfire. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAWg4vM1fCNqvm4Btu09EaNRcV9GTAN6qOSch_FIAypaFlpziJ0sFx0R52ml1kI43mmFd7q3ayTDdfatCRGCRqpmSnHGmPheQHyohOYFbqtHWhGACK7BTpYtdC3KMOb6j35Z0vxjKYGGtMFk56dJ6wXGwXiYM0q7xRWZZ24i2LFLf6SC2m0SSqXnXmYU8TC8IuXX_VVsHlCADvdlR314dFaPyln1nNRb1Ag=>  


Cracking Pinterest


Pinterest-the social scrapbooking site and purveyor of eye-candy-has millions of people window-shopping its images. Reuters' Beth Pinsker and Mitch Lipka explain why retailers are still stumped, though, when it comes to monetizing all that user engagement. "Retailers are hankering after these users, but it is sometimes difficult to nab them because Pinterest is an ad-free website and 'pins' flourish virally." One of the best ways to reach followers on the site, note Pinsker and Lipka, is to "do anything but try to sell products." Find out more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAUnQ4tOHzjCSKcTJCThZDpXXyViL0CCcGXhFQRjGem38q2_vOtOY4MkTdlNpLMV2JDOCwbJbPekYxxw_t5Qw3ZUL2H87eOGfFr5eZ8_TTM5no_zlg32gUGodzHapRX57M7UCU8Q291e66z5nwXrqSWJcYT5DD6Jqdua9pTdBTRrBrrPwfhFNxvUJaScnku40McWy1Ta4zQpgMM-yB8LdPJl>

Amazon Ad Network


Amazon wants to build an ad app network as their new API emphasizes. See it on Amazon's developer site <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAXBgvygk5XH5TbK_lbItKei7W6v6MKPd4V033sgwiY6y61E12jCLo7w5zBNBQhRg1HYdMS9XMh_v4yQ0nN6ILhFzzClf7ITg0A6IqtodQEYPcYDL96VaHU6G3ynU6tuSmZb5KiESuOOQQ==> . Serving The Store - Online


Helping marketers alert shoppers on their mobile devices when a certain product is available in stores and showing them where they can buy it is a growing business. And local marketing and commerce platform Retailigence is looking to take advantage with a new $6.3 million round of funding. The company says the cash will be used to further expand its platform in service to brick-and-mortar stores. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAWfHnFEfjogXz11K38VZmMivTpucospoQgzzpm0fxcPNjEG_I9Yml3czHrKvvNw76xpgL5WwdSeqgVunJH5vqRFv50qUKkSsdSYpb6_XnWUlULZOBPzgTY_TL4lqJVK3fNgNHTPHHKVosKCJDA-q568qK3sQXf7O92nT72XfStobiuujUZKP1f2n81d4HhOhdFxJtjohjMw0dp4qnZ6xh6V1uOGUQNRLij4JWEtkpPnfg==> 


Google's Prime Time Challenge


Techcrunch's Alexia Tsotsis reports that Google is quietly prepping a lower-cost challenger to Amazon Prime, which offers shoppers unlimited video content in exchange for a discounted shopping membership. Dubbed Google Shopping Express, the service will, according to an unidentified Techcrunch source, will be "$10 or $15 cheaper than Amazon Prime, offer same-day delivery from brick-and-mortar stores like Target, Walmart, Walgreens and Safeway." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAUZsmfiO3bSygLp8rUcAcXMgV5_OFmCgY8KIpjYRDjXxP7n2JQCtdiIZk157fLuiA1uB4jNFmAhDAvZUEziKsfxYwiLxj10gDqd0crSqPrBBE7MCz6aLAIFcUPPlzltxq8kdxgLNI77Vfes74pU1PTVgAlSY7qJ0Qr07LVYTyUWq0dacTVqhdo-wTRlOqYH7YDkPZUOsSWSAJvqCVLzu0iDTBO2wPH3npyqhIQkjXXQkTRolyWSSwP2UEdDknxpqkg661ojkdUe9mQMvftt4ADdH4xwFiFwuPJ3Gc-Mcm-n3Ka28b9_Gor1Wk_l0tD3SpGfiDt1lkx1vyuemt0HdeI5wPoi-axi9sMkTrI5KsNi7V6N8tohwVpI> . Oh, and that offline purchase data is a nice extra. 


Online Radio Ads: On!


Pandora has been looking at how to approach programmatic ad sales methods for the past year and an agreement with Strata Marketing and Mediaocean that will allow clients of the media-buying software providers to view the digital radio player's customer segments appears to be a step in that direction. The news comes two days ahead of Pandora's Q4 earnings, not too coincidentally. "Pandora has data that's more granular than any panel can be," Mediaocean CEO Bill Wise told Adweek's Chris Heine. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001wo2SgmutEAV2h6oWQwas0SAIRkaidvGhZtlytElteSr1UPLPCRKITtl4G-AoHLI8wZtl1SPcrx3iBMxhkA0HrI1yiS4LoLeeE_VjABaiMU1hm3d62e_tWAG88w41ZtDacUK-oEkSFwVyUIDCKfvknhz5ROHU887_1Mo6S8X-oB9JifxuoH9zDart8MpqAQTrR6PSqm6evc3qI6WDv2P0aA==> .

Native Ad Clutter


Riffing on a piece by NY Times writer Nick Bilton about declining engagement rates <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd_9AHv-NtLo0TKN0XzduEe80kqMMGqWLi-TQwyIFOKR3QHuUSNyyU_8EUKLQVQM0E-kSYuQ2kc_KuvnchfkE9uXljjuCKJvQUQSv4Q3sWs6BGc840B0ZewMIbhj-AP7G0pCGNcMcwBOH7mlkekSA-lEa0ih0J0H2iPkuOuiVcD0elVT02TortFn2E3tkfYJumjZfGjoquHESLu_f_wamOddE>  among his Facebook subscribers, TechCrunch's Josh Constine wonders at the "skittish gift horse" that is the newsfeed. "The volume of advertising in the feed has increased dramatically this year ...It's a balancing act, and Facebook may be tipping too far towards advertisers' interests right now. Facebook risks alienating users if the feed's meritocracy is poisoned with paid marketing and users feel like they're not seeing what they want." Will the pendulum swinging back to adjacent, non-native placements? Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd__fXkysp5mCfh531aeylK7ci6POfsltdrw5pWcLvZ2LnkuxnfGTidqMxUEWv2lYwgQOBAMPXFzItWfLVAe8RFmiDi9BIesAkdmVPF_ZTNfiUtTuy4SF6YIqCh8ftZzHh-RQp99W217QhDnigbZN667qPYGTdVQjPTQ=> 


Viewability Slog?


AdWeek gives viewable impressions the rough treatment in a piece on challenges to the IAB's Making Measurement Make Sense (3MS) initiative. "Instead of rallying around a new ad currency, questions continue to arise over the most practical of issues, such as how to measure, implement and enforce viewable impressions-and whether the whole conversation is even worthwhile." AdExchanger's take: Setting standards is often cumbersome and thankless, but buy-side momentum for viewability will push the process forward. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd__oUeIMPBx0bUHHUKSHHjSo-4FC1DdVKnDEd6bDwDP1epNHXOegP3W8eLQHsUoZXalf0QGnlT7SXnnmN3kq9IAslcOfxYQGhasVJ4YTx_2a0MmBZQcdLMiZYXT6hgifne3FlBDQSjt3LDou4VZrk70K5oSF0NNbMMWYWSGWhdGHYFPVA9PgOeR4OEgKJsCXllHt9hWL59cO-Q==> 


Adobe and Razorfish


Razorfish and Adobe have partnered on an expansion of the agency's marketing technology platform, Fluent. The deal, which also includes Publicis sibling agency DigitasLBi, enhances access to the Adobe Marketing Cloud. AdAge says, "Although Adobe works with many digital agencies, this is the first time it has entered a partnership in which the digital shop will develop its own marketing solution built on top of Adobe's Marketing Cloud." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd__r1erP6EjvxruV-PtZsh_RZnSu8QP0v8ypC5fld_ELzZ-3RWPbesZnuG6VbV7oM4xW3pCOmFGJjPPpk3CUThr5xJErULrvKT9IXgqa6brcRRuSJGHNcbeUhJJF8ptg6dlndlyhdqCOX2-jFRG1qoKds6cejVKV-RgrSnH-ebD3BMkh0CAND-IBudsHxXlhRT4uiOPY0Kew8ed1Pru4ubuyz4QNpRZ62Vg=>  Or read the press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd_9_l6mnGbocotqVz39z8Z6XN0bKhj5O9t5p2kU0TaK6A5kgojqcNEWecqvEWe5lRvcc9q7o34McQbOPdweSW8tXQrPQWKm_o2Sl3KGKGWholt1XQ2SEW1r5XRFsgEvagDaw1w1Kcis1zt0p9TWGXhw1Dx3KzIk1oE22SU9cj6Ud97q8bKlfOfNHQ8SYoEcTrfc=> . 


YouTube's Ad Revenue Issues


AllThingsD's Peter Kafka asks whether YouTube can generate enough ad dollars to support its premium programming and compete with traditional television. "According to people in and outside of YouTube, last year the site ended up with a glut of inventory, which put even more pressure on ad rates." Given YouTube's resources, it will deliver better ad vehicles sooner or later, but this could leave an opportunity for other video-hosting platforms to swoop in. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd_-7YkoZEfuxd-NnA-mxxvGIvm27mxOwtITpCTYO17ykMHLQs5LrsrSG2lZaQmOS_SVdsETQYkZZg-Xn4T4y5BieOIQj90g-hJu5gxhU30a-plJeyqyICcBNT3Tw-z0Uoh4k4geg5zjcagutdRSDioMMhqtgZrfyrgmTWU7A61Hyhw==> 


Lead Gen, Made 'Hotter'


The business of lead generation is generally still frowned upon as a residue from the analog days of direct marketing lists. Or worse, a regulatory tripwire for bribing consumers to "click here now." But McKinsey's Mike Lamb and Shawn Lankton, writing in the Harvard Business Review, offer a path to smarter, hotter -- and less crass -- lead gen."You don't have to choose between advertising and generating leads; you can pursue both at once," the duo advise. "Nor do you have to alienate your existing advertisers. Instead, renegotiate and show them they will get better value by paying you to deliver hot leads as well as show ads." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd_-uD7jVZ9r7q2qY6O9seohj-OpOFDCiJlD4e1il1PIHeAx0a7EOS7lYBN93_ygxBF5Y9PbRe6YpuVddFbXNe-IqVsHaKpSB86n2NB-IfqPsbfuYSlir5GPXgFURIqkYqw1myezQcHGbi7g1oNMvdwDgzw3Qy9vD11Q=> .

Lonely Planet Packs Its Bags?


After six years as parent of the Lonely Planet publisher of print and digital travel guides, the BBC is close to selling the property to Kentucky tycoon and conservationist Brad Kelley for roughly $100 million, reports Skift's Rafat Ali. Like a lot of traditional publishers, Lonely Planet has struggled to balance its print and digital businesses the last few years. "With LP, Kelley's team is likely thinking of the long-term value of the brand and investing in digital - especially video," Ali writes, citing unidentified sources. Nevertheless, BBC says all this is premature and that LP isn't traveling anywhere yet. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd__piL4X8PuKko60WKrZ9rkofSylIwcebGfsI28CGSOU72IsoqM7fZBZZxNiNfWTfFKzV3ItOuiMP2rXYO8gNlb2MwfUuxYmqsPPiqtnrDe6yRkW-HDfMgxOkqfkgwrJUw25oOT-yNMnyfZCPvn5Je11GGC_OIaLvZP-0vOr_vuLUGi1T1a9KshztL2uubjsxTEFaGMxRRDViQ618KZV6F4P> . 


Yodle Buys


Small biz marketing platform Yodle has snapped up LightHouse Practice Management Group, a marketing automation and CRM system used by dentists. "Adding online relationship marketing to our product offerings is the natural next step," said Yodle CEO Court Cunningham in a statement. Press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd_8pB5T5K3RWJu4d8nLIC0ASkvxESZQa2ML6gBf9kg6bXDjCjRKgz_EzjzHdKUx5Ti1HYKt5IzGwB5bouCQ6mjJyA-LwjEYi1Igbrb2Tj8cgHEgf5zAqXJ4F2_M0lf4zL3NnrRD5CAyy_-OHTj9Yz1TImWEW6ZYgpr0YYAOoOLRPB7v9CbVI9T6w0IhKLAvjaWVgRceJkfEE5LVuOX4WbSGj> .


Cross-Platform Guarantees


Whoa. Look at you, ABC/Disney. According to the NY Times' Media Decoder blog, ABC/Disney will offer guarantees across online and TV to advertisers courtesy of Nielsen's Online Campaign Ratings system. Take that comScore. NYT's Bill Carter explains, "The Nielsen service will provide detailed information on online viewing in two ways, [says] Steve Hasker, the president of Global Products for Nielsen. One is information that will go to the advertisers about the reach of specific ad campaigns. 'If an auto maker places ads on all different platforms, on television and online, we'll be able to measure all the people that see that particular campaign,' Mr. Hasker said. That will be possible because the commercials will carry a specific tag to identify them." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001YqUJnniCd__M2WSXtq_vljZoKJMA7LmcynRzhxPCcu1eJCPqYKauuao6lS7hrSz3NFG3U5yJ_yEdm-9_FbUOREhchMyCCAyXdcsvDBF-MEEGXhNzdCXWAYHXAotytuUpBnh5G2rr-NAuJ-KRRphBfRN5ZTT84Hv0n3YpXJzMxRRzwXEUs6FpVZRAvBEVEsNxZsJD_awuNfHxT_3SGLBfbPChTokTqXCJWahGL6u3tl3KSHpY5kotrA==>

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>   

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fKUgB_3Cuoyv-cuFo9E-sMp6l0HhmRhSSi6Fs3u6ncPKsQ08hJyZUKF87HzjbqiqR5feB53a6XCnLyJ8gNgi8bSNlUuQ20D-xFWPrVineTah_yRDx9LLfF6IlgDHA9khAE=> .

 

Optimizing The Content Algo


In The NY Times, David Carr recounts how movie streaming/DVD service Netflix used insights on its own "big data" to create a successful new television (wait, streaming) series called "House of Cards" with director David Fincher and actor Kevin Spacey. Carr writes, "Netflix, which has 27 million subscribers in the nation and 33 million worldwide, ran the numbers. It already knew that a healthy share had streamed the work of Mr. Fincher, the director of 'The Social Network,' from beginning to end. And films featuring Mr. Spacey had always done well, as had the British version of 'House of Cards.' With those three circles of interest, Netflix was able to find a Venn diagram intersection that suggested that buying the series would be a very good bet on original programming." Target the content <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fK4k_m5UhqaJkVMMIpxSPjGcT4esgwfufuAh6ldT3Z4SQgteGJclSMb_2ugumUKaItCDxOL-IJ2sZTIBC2k4-PkQP-Q5cncyyXbGXnPTF-LhVayzVYUk4azuWOcEjmqflv476FrK8Q2N5tObqR4zUFQIynaBoI5C0jhNW4UFs32W-PfuwDZ1kQp4QBBp_aZycNRU0MbSI6HONh8aHrsSc9J7yP0n_8jgZh_6k1kf_lpZQ==> . 


Exec Rumor Mill


The Business Insider reports that former Yahoo Rich Riley (LinkedIn <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fLVqIlwBOYZhr5IR7Mh9mTNjXsVQfZI5JroI7YuDXVbvVIgbj1ZbzB_QmrQ7AwBLHRUBhDVsClzNLDe6T-JJ-RnitsGtqq0CXw_PMovmJllvl6Q3KIGnP-8moztt2BsOCTlQjyVvpN9UmIx2FX0H9Vr> ), who had been with Yahoo for 13 years until he left last June, may become the next CEO of display ad retargeting firm Criteo. BI's Owen Thomas sees a tie-in to a Criteo IPO, "By hiring Riley, Criteo would simultaneously make itself more valuable to public investors, with a reassuringly experienced and well-connected CEO - and to Yahoo as an acquisition." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fJhqtamOTgmNIRiFCtjui7vkcNCPoybiRWM8oq_hycxWSCRA-yulBaiea2zBCSlIhns2uJc3rj-KkBJySSFrrpRNLMzs6z9QKDlqjby9pK6ViXVFja1mRtbimzQ6uRW-GqPE82QdNC7DcXDJsiPWegRy14fmtE9oYk=>  Yahoo buys Criteo? Seems unlikely. Yahoo CEO Marissa Mayer does not appear to be in ad tech acquisition mode. 


Mobile Display Takeover


The display ad world expands into mobile apps and Yelp is climbing aboard. Ad Age's Josh McDermott says it's all about "direct" as Yelp will be selling category takeovers: "InterContinental Hotels Group (IHG) and Taco Bell will be exclusive advertisers within their given Yelp category, meaning all ads served while Yelpers make travel-related searches will be from IHG while Taco Bell will serve all ads in the restaurant category." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fKF6UTy_KmXhv1lkPXJ90w9--v6a4Dn6_wkeTCJTGUX9lsHYAA6-yXfi3Spt2TIIcX5GMlfEN8ULa1drKtu2f5-gK8elUCKZEB8Rd2rdA9_mBlf6kPe0_qByYY2sEeSxnApM8c05Me8Z6vwDj7ykq86PhyXr3zibOl7_kTKu8Sr0db5Q0wLscmdqDQG3XLHxZE=>  Editor's note: It will be interesting to see if Yext <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fL6jif_UxFpi6tpEql1pzkJravS9EuJv5djHCHJsuNOTzf4Z14S8clUIV5PEkM64DX8iYX359KNihGsYEmdHOmGL_ObchQOLQs=>  can get in this mix. With its unified delivery of merchant information across Yelp and Yelp-like sites, its pipes could enable unique, retargetable addressability. Yext CEO Howard Lerman and Chairman Mike Walrath <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fJCzvh7vJvmBOjsnvZWcNRbVEl_a3PPJzYWq1t1JfFfVJGoJeJpClScaMPcSlN6w88HhbIbNb8hmKKQTCusXcy1uljXow3kxnXAECuA8NcvNpEyATU-O02i>  (former Right Media CEO) should be able to figure that one out. 


Real-Time Creative


Spongecell CEO Ben Kartzman pulls one right from his company's playbook in a think piece on MediaPost. He identifies the spawn of real-time bidding (RTB) as RTC - or real-time creative. Kartzman writes, "RTC draws upon the same Big Data technology as RTB - cookie matching, tracking tags, IP addresses and more - to deliver images and words appropriate for a particular viewer. It is relevant content tailored instantaneously and delivered seamlessly - a marketer's dream." Live the dream. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fJm4IDJRJ1yA9qgkU7jnBbqTLELgDI4uBzKcWfRu45LFOgLEJja0Uv5YR1YiU8kzygZgUY3ptMCkuCylZ3C6UnnTRb0mDANlr5GNIdO8wdsH3uzUo90QAbEtCV_Iew-9IBCaS7JZw_iXIsbfF9uc4IqbYE56JFFzYDCxLMeJeZ3DJPj5txzY140G4l6Gx52nNmkORWaNGwQZaAmz7VXqMV5lANrHROcqG8=> 


Around The Middleman


Gannett's Chief Digital Officer tells Digiday that he believes he has a solution to "middlemen" (i.e. ad networks, exchanges, etc.) who have eaten away at his newspaper sites' margins. Digiday's Alex Kantrowitz explains, "Instead of fitting as many ads as possible around an article, it decided to place a single ad unit next to each of the site's articles and package the content and ad together in a pop-out lightbox." Scarcity, integration... Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fIZxsDuHXK6ACcp5LYkde3ZOYBq2nvUgkfDupEfLa4CnhCebzpUPjL-WkM36kI9_A2u4GXGRxg81GrlgGE_ak7sbj_92Vryj_Y_XpocGo-fMtcilfdzK0KgIUMUtPoDaTZJa85x-Rag-JqxBhGiR8GoPBNmCCjfd5gtYW2H5L17La93JVKM_kXa> .

Cutting The PII


Ad network industry org Network Advertising Initiative has come out with new guidelines for its members according to an NAI blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fKC3eBePMRNTqeyGhaCssffYls4MX3aPztRQ0dliF2fwLhVHtXx3I9v54V_9YdWARaE4djBSQSIMZESIADfOZJbSbgJNuvfjlmJ--w-PpT-XgwZWQyf-jboVAlQjftQDteWn7t48zET9nEwMa1-oDJUIKUZpZ_KBGqXeCJVQRrZVZvp16wbjFpirsrvgFsNEoM=> . MediaPost's Wendy Davis deciphers the changes saying that clear definitions around PII (personally identifiable information) and non-PII and its use in digital ads are at the core. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fKkmIkqBt7Y3nofARvODSI3j0_DDScofoCwf3axejvXX8ZXrfseVsqvFDKnbrOdFBiLNVikRrX_YCJVDEvdmIJzjsrghqMwNa9kv8zn5huQubIQf7rGcAcYihT8hfjeUUZVU6KwskLbE5GmmMPVsFGkqrjDSwtcryDU87OKAjJK3HEg6QZ7Rum01EYBxeXdDk2-P5G49lhI2ADF8r3FwKDFpUuO092WRNA=> . 


'I'm Moving'


On Friday, AppNexus CTO Mike Nolet announced that he's loading up the truck and moving to London. From the AppNexus blog, he offers some explanation including that both he and his wife are of European descent and clarifies that his role will not change with the company. Nolet adds, "Europe is a hugely strategic market for us, and broad, international expansion is one of our core priorities." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fI1uRKu1KT7O9kcOvOPd5J-xg5u_KZmPKybBpx4Qv8OKKxLKyn0myPg-Yeta-yZf4BAs2mD4CDqbWp_Yqf-PZUJhC4QsN0i7a6d2f7uN3AJQQRC8Pv5V4I5fcrwIAQdTQuNFGGPuwLrsw==>  Whatever the reasons, AppNexus will be pouring fuel on the European RTB fires where AppNexus partners abound. 


Adding RTB


In Europe, performance marketing agency LeadMedia announced last week that it has acquired ad tech company Gamned to help with efforts across real-time bidded ad inventory. All of the 29-person, Paris-based Gamned team will join LeadMedia's 150 employees. Read the release (PDF). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001P36t41bE_fJj2E92gdWhAW5CUSir3pALk_vzKtsQHaypiKX91na9W7nD2EUNHcfohKZKe6esSmUH5tDPx6r9E47Ab3Bdm3glAwrZtoE-oU7KHkK1gbt7PbchFgWaAGbq37wUmgm-ZcR9M7Yrz034jMLAFYQvqp5cepTO4Xqubz3GQ4zTHa4IorRhYsg2meaclLnquNZpRcjbTibmrjHyXw==>  LeadMedia had 25.6 million in net revenues in 2012 (US$ 33 million), an increase of 34% compared to 2011, according to a company spokesperson.

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?

AOL's Latest Shuffle


AOL CEO Tim Armstrong has often talked about the company's one constant: change and more of the same. Whether it's rebranding business divisions or moving executives from one department to another, nothing at AOL stays the same for long. Artie Minson, despite having been promoted less than a year ago to COO from CFO, has been there for years and was noted for helping manage AOL's spin-off from Time Warner. But he's going to be leaving the company as his responsibilities were reduced after AOL divided its business into three separate operating groups: Brand, Network and Membership. The Brand Group has had difficulty building up revenues for its owned & operated sites, including Patch, though progress has been made. To speed things along, AOL has named media veteran -- and AOL board member -- Susan Lyne as CEO of the Brand Group. "In her roles as CEO then Chairman of Gilt, and previously as President and CEO of Martha Stewart Living Omnimedia, Susan has a proven track record of brand building and aggressive growth," Armstrong said. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OFdCPwv3K6Id9okX69FiwqyvxPtTJ50DWflu3nr_wIneKp0df0RgQOASJHE42q0XPn1DhZ6VavWNdY8SZO2p-XdJjxh1r9fw_RPsj9U_VrroqdWvFtafERzrfKtv6XBGK71a_LU-632qGFH-rUa59TOG_MvBgtunTh1zlpVjhiaAR5aCjPrRjY3VhpLDORj_IgzB-IhHGLJ3i6FZbNUaNQ==> . 


Groupon's Bad Deal


Daily deals site Groupon disappointed shareholders and board members with another lackluster earnings report. And as a result, CEO Andrew Mason is stepping down and the board is conducting a search for a replacement. Mason is stepping down, as he apparently had run out of time to lessen the company's reliance on digital coupons. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OFdCPwv3K6I3P6kIo4l0E6CnWkchmn-9F28weXhID9m1J_bguquhxKNb9MuFKEToOTSF-dGYUJQAv8ZJ-lgi675eJK4ltBXKc4Ot9hdZ4i5INEX7cPMBYb8szHEGAFTzSM0YlZ3x2MKd2hb5bYmkZOg1Qi1J_CYpM21zF2596v4=> . The last straw was when Groupon missed revenue estimates of $640.2 million, as sales were $638.3 million, Bloomberg's Douglas MacMillan reported."This is still a big work in process for them to transform from just a daily deal business to a local e-commerce engine," said Edward Woo, an analyst at Ascendiant Capital Markets. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OFdCPwv3K6IvOnUeseXUDGaWkEX3u72ZmvwQFf8WpWDIDZky4JKwEUcEkfi5jENrMXiRFueYRiTUEwLVnChqWfO8dxcUpfwx3YInJ83GoPVHj05kEj-YwRnpxznURUDy3D1KoZQcxsVg7gcDTXgoDrRy9INWWFvPJhgzvK39L3Yxb5gjGXlyV23y_dpSWBwONt9G6x7Tg1nqtAOOA2wXQohLYaThUvfisMJBnE7SfHg=> . 


Cookie Love


Turn SVP of Product Joshua Koran says that recent changes to prevent cookie tracking of users in Mozilla is a step in the wrong direction (Turn's business relies, in part, on cookie tracking). He writes in Ad Age, "With the Firefox plan, Mozilla is making a unilateral decision without giving consumers a choice, and blocking even the collection of this anonymous data. We are steadfast advocates for consumer rights and hope that as with other anti-competitive actions, this initiative will be rethought in light of the impact it could have on the online advertising industry and on small publishers." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OFdCPwv3K6J3PGvuyEaAn5Iinu8X2dD7f8cbmjaxcvUlT3vz-GxZxCyUlbo-Traj4x5rudkB-MPZoqOov2HEF-mC5V4U7V_ePnX2vi1U1mKJlxMwH-_NXkCpivbCeMkFgQ-xKoIkG2KBVZ74Uue0PPy5grdN1TGXuiLuO1C9Y5deWs8zDWHrM-kshK2TmPLp>  In related news, Adweek reports <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OFdCPwv3K6IPtW8mo_0Vqbv-VKS4CvcmlPsW5u8OUp3QVOMniFsRAIUTb6i7btmCRMgztv0p4BGXqlvETzRnf59gP5LSuttkqS6bR8zjdnDX4TdnRVWOUX-RB8Iv4nqn9HYX0xHnBv2kj_YB3X9CMuX030pzUWhjLV-04DK2eZ7k5rvU0RrFVPq4ZUhkVHJOhTA-8f-p-ss=>  that U.S. Senator Rockefeller is reviving Do-Not-Track legislation. 


The Publisher Agency


In Digiday, Jack Marshall notes the publisher trend of building its own agency (Hearst, Meredith, Conde Nast). Matt Britton, CEO of social agency MRY, tells Marshall, "Every publisher knows that they can't build a sustainable business through media agencies. Publishers know they need to try to create direct relationships with brands, and, yes, that puts agencies at risk." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OFdCPwv3K6KzqeWT_jySsOzgqCdXHVYcHGLrN_1nlw3ezcMs4greFr_8WLVOUzdjF1_-Q5Z-uCQZrtLGemDwEHROhaIHnklBHmFoIt1TxxYf0UtRfQVzq9XpKf5q7kmcfW6jB1UfvkVbE1Tlc0V5pI7vMT4b6KcNMAHhJcyPXZI=>
